二、研究内容和方法

Ⅰ. Research Framework

This study proposes a theoretical framework linking AI literacy to upward influence behavior, grounded in Resource Dependence Theory (Pfeffer & Salancik, 1978) and informed by Tripathi's (2021) extension to employee-supervisor relationships.

[Insert Figure 1: Research Framework]

Research Propositions:

P1: AI literacy positively relates to employees' perceived resource advantage.
P2: Perceived resource advantage enables employees to engage in upward influence behavior.
P3: Perceived resource advantage mediates the relationship between AI literacy and upward influence behavior.
P4: Supervisor openness moderates the relationship between perceived resource advantage and upward influence behavior.

Ⅱ. Research Methodology

This study employs the following research methods:

(1) Literature Review

This study systematically reviews domestic and international literature on Resource Dependence Theory, AI literacy, and upward influence behavior to establish the theoretical framework and identify research gaps.

(2) Semi-structured Interview

In-depth interviews will be conducted with 15-20 Generation Z knowledge workers. Participants must meet the following criteria: born between 1995-2010, at least 6 months of full-time work experience, and regular use of AI tools at work. Each interview lasts 45-60 minutes and will be audio-recorded with participant consent. The interview covers four core themes: AI literacy, perceived resource advantage, upward influence behavior, and supervisor openness.

(3) Thematic Analysis

Interview data will be analyzed using Braun and Clarke's (2006) six-phase thematic analysis approach to identify key themes and develop theoretical interpretations.

AI: [2025-12-05 07:25:46]
Ⅰ. Research Framework

This study proposes a theoretical framework linking AI literacy to upward influence behavior, grounded in Resource Dependence Theory (Pfeffer & Salancik, 1978) and informed by Tripathi's (2021) extension to employee-supervisor relationships.

[Insert Figure 1: Research Framework]

Research Propositions:

P1: AI literacy positively relates to employees' perceived resource advantage.
P2: Perceived resource advantage enables employees to engage in upward influence behavior.
P3: Perceived resource advantage mediates the relationship between AI literacy and upward influence behavior.
P4: Supervisor openness moderates the relationship between perceived resource advantage and upward influence behavior.

Ⅱ. Research Methodology

This study employs the following research methods:

(1) Literature Review

This study systematically reviews domestic and international literature on Resource Dependence Theory, AI literacy, and upward influence behavior to establish the theoretical framework and identify research gaps. This method is essential for grounding the research in existing theory and identifying the specific contributions this study can make.

(2) Semi-structured Interview

In-depth interviews will be conducted with 15-20 Generation Z knowledge workers. Participants must meet the following criteria: born between 1995-2010, at least 6 months of full-time work experience, and regular use of AI tools at work. Each interview lasts 45-60 minutes and will be audio-recorded with participant consent.

This qualitative approach is appropriate because the phenomenon under investigation—how AI literacy translates into organizational influence—is relatively novel and requires in-depth exploration of mechanisms and processes that quantitative methods may not capture (Creswell & Poth, 2018).

The interview guide is developed based on established frameworks: AI literacy questions draw on Zhong et al.'s (2024) three-dimensional framework (AI Knowledge, AI Affectivity, AI Thinking); upward influence behavior questions are informed by Kipnis et al.'s (1980) influence tactics; and supervisor openness questions adapt Detert and Burris's (2007) conceptualization.

(3) Thematic Analysis

Interview data will be analyzed using Braun and Clarke's (2006) six-phase thematic analysis approach to identify key themes and develop theoretical interpretations. This method allows for systematic identification of patterns across interviews while remaining sensitive to participants' own meanings and experiences.
